<p>The <b>2016 Green Party presidential primaries</b> were a series of <a href="/wiki/Primary_election" title="Primary election">primaries</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caucuses" class="mw-redirect" title="Caucuses">caucuses</a> and <a href="/wiki/Party_conference" title="Party conference">state conventions</a> in which voters elected delegates to represent a candidate for the <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_of_the_United_States" title="Green Party of the United States">Green Party</a>'s nominee for <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">President of the United States</a> at the <a href="/wiki/2016_Green_National_Convention" title="2016 Green National Convention">2016 Green National Convention</a>. The primaries, held in numerous states on various dates from January to July 2016, featured elections publicly funded and held as an alternative ballot, concurrent with the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_presidential_primaries,_2016" title="Democratic Party presidential primaries, 2016">Democratic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_presidential_primaries,_2016" title="Republican Party presidential primaries, 2016">Republican primaries</a>, and elections privately funded by the Green Party, held non-concurrently with the major party primaries. Over 400 delegates to the Green National Convention were elected in these primaries, with a candidate needing a simple majority of these delegates to become the party's nominee for president.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A total of six candidates stood in the primaries, including the preceding Green nominee for president in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_2012" title="United States presidential election, 2012">2012 presidential election</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jill_Stein" title="Jill Stein">Jill Stein</a>, who <a href="/wiki/Jill_Stein_presidential_campaign,_2016" title="Jill Stein presidential campaign, 2016">sought the nomination for a second time</a>. Other candidates included Sedinam Kinamo Christin Moyowasifza Curry, who had previously worked as a campaign manager for the <a href="/wiki/Cynthia_McKinney_presidential_campaign,_2008" title="Cynthia McKinney presidential campaign, 2008">presidential campaign</a> of the Green Party's 2008 nominee, <a href="/wiki/Cynthia_McKinney" title="Cynthia McKinney">Cynthia McKinney</a>, in addition to singer-songwriter and <a href="/wiki/Earth_First!" title="Earth First!">Earth First!</a> activist <a href="/wiki/Darryl_Cherney" title="Darryl Cherney">Darryl Cherney</a>, <a href="/wiki/Perennial_candidate" title="Perennial candidate">perennial candidate</a> <a href="/wiki/Kent_Mesplay" class="mw-redirect" title="Kent Mesplay">Kent Mesplay</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_South_Carolina" title="University of South Carolina">University of South Carolina</a> professor William Kreml, and youth rights activist Elijah Manley.
</p><p>Formal recognition is a requirement to be the Green Party's nominee.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>  On May 4, the Green Party of the United States formally recognized William Kreml and <a href="/wiki/Jill_Stein" title="Jill Stein">Jill Stein</a> as candidates for its presidential nomination.  On June 15, the Stein campaign announced that it had received 203 delegates, enough to win the nomination on the first ballot at the National Convention. Jill Stein formally won the nomination on August 6, during the <a href="/wiki/2016_Green_National_Convention" title="2016 Green National Convention">2016 Green National Convention</a><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As the Green Party presidential candidate in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_2016" title="United States presidential election, 2016">United States presidential election, 2016</a> Stein received 1,457,222 votes or 1.06% of the popular vote.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Stein received zero electoral college votes.
</p>

<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jill_Stein_OWS_S17.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Jill_Stein_OWS_S17.jpg/220px-Jill_Stein_OWS_S17.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Jill_Stein_OWS_S17.jpg/330px-Jill_Stein_OWS_S17.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Jill_Stein_OWS_S17.jpg/440px-Jill_Stein_OWS_S17.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jill_Stein_OWS_S17.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Jill Stein speaks at an <a href="/wiki/Occupy_Wall_Street" title="Occupy Wall Street">Occupy Wall Street</a> demonstration in September 2012, during her campaign for the presidency as the Green Party's nominee.</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_2016" title="United States presidential election, 2016">2016 United States presidential election</a> will be the fourth to be contested by the Green Party of the United States since they split from the <a href="/wiki/Greens/Green_Party_USA" title="Greens/Green Party USA">Greens/Green Party USA</a> (G/GPUSA) in 2001. The <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election" title="United States presidential election">2004 presidential election</a> saw Green nominee <a href="/wiki/David_Cobb" title="David Cobb">David Cobb</a> appear on ballots in 27 states plus the <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">District of Columbia</a>, and received 0.10% of the popular vote, losing out to many other candidates and parties on the ballot, including third-placed independent <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Nader" title="Ralph Nader">Ralph Nader</a>, who had been the presidential nominee of the G/GPUSA in the 1996 and 2000 elections.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_2008" title="United States presidential election, 2008">2008 election</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cynthia_McKinney" title="Cynthia McKinney">Cynthia McKinney</a> was nominated as the Green Party's candidate for the presidency and had ballot access to 32 states plus DC. However, McKinney insignificantly improved upon Cobb's performance, capturing only 0.12% of the popular vote in an election that also saw Nader finish a strong third behind the Democratic and Republican parties.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Having received minimal publicity in the previous elections, thus contributing to the low voting share that the party received, the Green Party gained significant exposure and media attention in the lead-up to the <a href="/wiki/2012_Green_National_Convention" title="2012 Green National Convention">2012 Green National Convention</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_2012" title="United States presidential election, 2012">2012 presidential election</a>, starting with media personality <a href="/wiki/Roseanne_Barr" title="Roseanne Barr">Roseanne Barr</a>'s announcement of her presidential run with the Green Party.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Using the publicity gained from the announcement, Barr praised the Green Party and championed their beliefs through interviews and public statements, which were often profane and harshly critical of both the Democratic and Republican parties.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Barr, however, lost the nomination at the 2012 Green National Convention to physician and activist <a href="/wiki/Jill_Stein" title="Jill Stein">Jill Stein</a>, who had gained the support of Green Party delegates through her "<a href="/wiki/Green_New_Deal" title="Green New Deal">Green New Deal</a>" platform of <a href="/wiki/Progressivism" title="Progressivism">progressive</a> economic policies centered on the prevention of future <a href="/wiki/Financial_crisis" title="Financial crisis">financial crisises</a> and the acceleration of <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">global warming</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-stein-npr_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stein-npr-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jill_Stein_presidential_campaign,_2012" title="Jill Stein presidential campaign, 2012">Stein's campaign for the presidency</a> focused mostly on keeping the publicity gained by the Green Party and gaining support from independents and dissenting Democratic and Republican voters, often echoing resentment towards the two parties.<sup id="cite_ref-stein-npr_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stein-npr-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> This included a court challenge against the <a href="/wiki/Commission_on_Presidential_Debates" title="Commission on Presidential Debates">Commission on Presidential Debates</a> by Stein that sought to include her in the official <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election_debates,_2012" class="mw-redirect" title="United States presidential election debates, 2012">presidential election debates</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Stein's campaign also gained media attention and exposure through a series of <a href="/wiki/Nonviolent_resistance" title="Nonviolent resistance">nonviolent protests</a>, including those against the presidential debates,<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Keystone_XL" class="mw-redirect" title="Keystone XL">Keystone XL pipeline</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Foreclosure" title="Foreclosure">foreclosures</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> which had Stein arrested, and even jailed, numerous times.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On election day, Stein oversaw a relatively sharp rise in the Green Party's popularity, earning 0.36% of the popular vote (469,628 votes), across the Green Party's ballot access in 36 states plus DC.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> The result was triple the amount Cynthia McKinney received in 2008, pushing the Green Party from a lower-tier third party to the second most popular third party, trailing behind the <a href="/wiki/Libertarian_Party_(United_States)" title="Libertarian Party (United States)">Libertarian Party</a>, who had nominated the popular former <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_New_Mexico" title="Governor of New Mexico">Governor of New Mexico</a> <a href="/wiki/Gary_Johnson" title="Gary Johnson">Gary Johnson</a> as their presidential candidate, also setting numerous Libertarian Party and presidential third party records.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> The election also notably made Stein the most successful <a href="/wiki/List_of_female_United_States_presidential_and_vice-presidential_candidates" title="List of female United States presidential and vice-presidential candidates">female presidential candidate in U.S. history</a>, surpassing <a href="/wiki/Lenora_Fulani" title="Lenora Fulani">Lenora Fulani</a>'s bid for the presidency in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1988" title="United States presidential election, 1988">1988 election</a>, with the <a href="/wiki/New_Alliance_Party" title="New Alliance Party">New Alliance Party</a>, who had ballot access in all states plus DC and earned 217,219 votes that year.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Despite her success, however, Stein's campaign was criticized by those who felt that she had failed to capitalise on her momentum and gain an even bigger success.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Candidates">Candidates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_presidential_primaries,_2016&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Candidates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The national <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_of_the_United_States" title="Green Party of the United States">Green Party of the United States</a> officially recognized two candidates, <a href="/wiki/Jill_Stein" title="Jill Stein">Jill Stein</a> and William Kreml,<sup id="cite_ref-Recognized_Candidates_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Recognized_Candidates-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> while four additional candidates have appeared on several state—or territory—ballots.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Results_by_state">Results by state</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_presidential_primaries,_2016&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Results by state">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/File:Green_Party_Presidential_Primaries_Results_2016.svg" class="image" title="First place (popular vote or delegate count)"><img alt="First place (popular vote or delegate count)" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Green_Party_Presidential_Primaries_Results_2016.svg/600px-Green_Party_Presidential_Primaries_Results_2016.svg.png" width="600" height="371" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Green_Party_Presidential_Primaries_Results_2016.svg/900px-Green_Party_Presidential_Primaries_Results_2016.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Green_Party_Presidential_Primaries_Results_2016.svg/1200px-Green_Party_Presidential_Primaries_Results_2016.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="959" data-file-height="593" /></a>
</p>
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #008000; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Jill Stein</div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Illinois_primary">Illinois primary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_presidential_primaries,_2016&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Illinois primary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Illinois Green Party primary was held between January 25 and February 17. Green Party members could vote online or could cast ballots at select caucus locations. Jill Stein won by a landslide with 86.9% of the vote.<sup id="cite_ref-illinois_results_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-illinois_results-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Massachusetts_primary">Massachusetts primary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_presidential_primaries,_2016&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Massachusetts primary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Massachusetts primary took place on March 1. Five candidates appeared on the ballot. Members of the party could apply to be delegates to be sent to the national convention until March 10 (over a week after the primary).<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> The number of voters that took part in the election slightly increased from the 1,554 that took part in the 2012 primary.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Minnesota_caucuses">Minnesota caucuses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_presidential_primaries,_2016&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Minnesota caucuses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Green Party of Minnesota held caucuses on March 1 in Saint Paul, Minneapolis, Bemidji, White Bear Lake, Blaine, Grand Rapids, and Willmar.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Jill Stein won the caucuses with 84.3% of the vote. The delegates apportioned to each candidate will be decided at the state convention in <a href="/wiki/St._Cloud,_Minnesota" title="St. Cloud, Minnesota">St. Cloud, Minnesota</a> in June.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> The results of the caucuses are as follows:<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Maine_caucuses">Maine caucuses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_presidential_primaries,_2016&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Maine caucuses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Maine held a series of caucuses throughout the state between February 27 and March 19. The Maine Green Independent Party compiled the results and assign delegates at the state convention on May 7.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On March 13, 2016 it was announced that Jill Stein had won the Maine Green Independent Party Caucuses.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> On May 7, the party announced Stein would receive 9 delegates, Sedinam Kinamo Christin Moyowasifza Curry would receive one, and the remaining delegate would be uncommitted.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arizona_primary">Arizona primary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_presidential_primaries,_2016&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Arizona primary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Arizona Green Party held its primary on March 22. Jill Stein won with 79.1% of the vote, and the overall number of voters that took place in the primary saw a 54% increase, from 573 in 2012 to 880 in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> Only two candidates qualified for the primary:<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Virginia_primary">Virginia primary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_presidential_primaries,_2016&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Virginia primary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Virginia Green Party held its primary from March 20 through April 3. The Green party calls this a primary. However this was not an open primary nor were voters statewide allowed to vote via ballot access. 
Primary elections are the means by which the general public can indicate their preference for a candidate in an upcoming general election or by-election.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>  This was not the case in Virginia as the general public had no access to the Primary process. In Virginia voters are not restricted party membership as in this process.
</p><p>Members were able to vote online through an email ballot or through the mail.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> This was therefore a closed primary. On April 13, it was announced that Jill Stein had won with 76% of the vote. The state's four delegates were apportioned at the May 28 state meeting.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Primaries in Virginia are reserved for the two major parties.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colorado_convention">Colorado convention</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_presidential_primaries,_2016&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Colorado convention">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On April 3, the <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_of_Colorado" title="Green Party of Colorado">Green Party of Colorado</a> held a presidential nominating convention in <a href="/wiki/Centennial,_Colorado" title="Centennial, Colorado">Centennial, Colorado</a> for registered Green voters.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ohio_convention">Ohio convention</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_presidential_primaries,_2016&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Ohio convention">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_of_Ohio" title="Green Party of Ohio">Green Party of Ohio</a> participated in the March 15 primaries in Ohio, though they did not hold their presidential primary during the event.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> Instead, delegates to the Green National Convention were awarded based on presidential preference through a nominating convention in Columbus on April 3. Members of the Green Party of Ohio were able to vote in the convention.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Young_Greens_Caucus">Young Greens Caucus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_presidential_primaries,_2016&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Young Greens Caucus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Green Party allows each of its <a href="/wiki/Identity_Caucus" class="mw-redirect" title="Identity Caucus">Identity Caucuses</a> to hold a presidential preference vote and award two delegates to the candidate that wins. The Young Greens Caucus, representing registered Greens below the age of 36, held an online vote from March 28 to April 5. Jill Stein won with 91.7% of the vote, her largest threshold of victory of the primary election so far, and was awarded both of the delegates representing the Young Greens.<sup id="cite_ref-Young_Greens_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Young_Greens-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Texas_conventions">Texas conventions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_presidential_primaries,_2016&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Texas conventions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Texas Green Party held its elections at conventions at the precinct level on March 8,<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> the county level on March 12,<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> and the district level on March 19,<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> leading up to the state nominating convention in <a href="/wiki/Grey_Forest,_Texas" title="Grey Forest, Texas">Grey Forest, Texas</a> on April 9 and 10.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On April 10 it was announced <a href="/wiki/Jill_Stein" title="Jill Stein">Jill Stein</a> had won the convention.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Oregon">Oregon</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_presidential_primaries,_2016&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Oregon">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>This state's Green Party held its convention on April 17 and its presidential preference vote on May 21. On May 22, it was announced that <a href="/wiki/Jill_Stein" title="Jill Stein">Jill Stein</a> had won the preference vote.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rhode_Island_convention">Rhode Island convention</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_presidential_primaries,_2016&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Rhode Island convention">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Green Party of Rhode Island held a meeting on May 21, 2016 in <a href="/wiki/Warwick,_Rhode_Island" title="Warwick, Rhode Island">Warwick, Rhode Island</a> to decide who their 4 delegates to the national convention will support.
</p><p>On May 24, it was announced that <a href="/wiki/Jill_Stein" title="Jill Stein">Jill Stein</a> would receive all four of this states delegates.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lavender_Greens_Caucus">Lavender Greens Caucus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_presidential_primaries,_2016&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Lavender Greens Caucus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lavender_Greens&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Lavender Greens (page does not exist)">Lavender Greens</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Identity_Caucus" class="mw-redirect" title="Identity Caucus">Identity Caucus</a> within the Green Party dedicated to lesbian, gay, bisexual, transgender, queer, intersex, and asexual (LGBTQIA) members, announced on June 1 that it was holding a discussion among its members over which candidate(s) will receive its two delegates. The caucus released a questionnaire filled out by candidates and directed members to a <a href="/wiki/Listserv" class="mw-redirect" title="Listserv">listserv</a> where they could discuss and vote for the candidate of their choice. The caucus announced that the discussion/voting would last two weeks.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Jill Stein won this presidential preference vote, and received both of the delegates.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Georgia_convention">Georgia convention</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_presidential_primaries,_2016&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Georgia convention">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="California_primary">California primary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_presidential_primaries,_2016&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: California primary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The California Green Party primary took place on June 7 with five candidates on the ballot.  <a href="/wiki/Jill_Stein" title="Jill Stein">Jill Stein</a> won the California primary.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>
The California <a href="/wiki/Peace_and_Freedom_Party" title="Peace and Freedom Party">Peace and Freedom Party</a> had asked for Jill Stein to also be listed on its presidential primary ballot, but the <a href="/wiki/California_Secretary_of_State" class="mw-redirect" title="California Secretary of State">California Secretary of State</a> left her off of their ballot and refused to release internal documents on the decision.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup></p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:California_Green_Presidential_Primary_Election_Results_by_County,_2016.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/California_Green_Presidential_Primary_Election_Results_by_County%2C_2016.svg/220px-California_Green_Presidential_Primary_Election_Results_by_County%2C_2016.svg.png" width="220" height="374" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/California_Green_Presidential_Primary_Election_Results_by_County%2C_2016.svg/330px-California_Green_Presidential_Primary_Election_Results_by_County%2C_2016.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/California_Green_Presidential_Primary_Election_Results_by_County%2C_2016.svg/440px-California_Green_Presidential_Primary_Election_Results_by_County%2C_2016.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="167" data-file-height="284" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:California_Green_Presidential_Primary_Election_Results_by_County,_2016.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>County results of the California Green presidential primary, 2016.<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="New_York_convention">New York convention</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_presidential_primaries,_2016&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: New York convention">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Green Party of New York State held a state nominating convention on June 11 in <a href="/wiki/Troy,_New_York" title="Troy, New York">Troy, New York</a> to allow members to vote for their preferred presidential candidate. Green Party members unable to attend the convention were able to vote absentee by mail.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Jill Stein received 89% of the vote at the GPNY convention, winning 16 delegates.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Maryland_primary">Maryland primary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_presidential_primaries,_2016&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Maryland primary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Green Party of Maryland began mailing ballots to those who requested them in May. The final vote and tabulation of the ballots took place at the state convention on June 12.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> Seven candidates appeared on the ballot: <a href="/wiki/Jill_Stein" title="Jill Stein">Jill Stein</a>, Kent Mesplay, <a href="/wiki/Darryl_Cherney" title="Darryl Cherney">Darryl Cherney</a>, Sedinam Curry, William Kreml, Elijah Manley, and Raymond Haigood.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>

<h3><span id="Washington.2C_D.C._primary"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Washington,_D.C._primary">Washington, D.C. primary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_presidential_primaries,_2016&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Washington, D.C. primary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Washington, DC, Green Party primary was set to take place on June 14. However, due to confusion during a change in leadership, the party missed the deadline for notifying the DC Board of Elections of the presidential candidates it wished to have listed on its primary ballot (local candidates for the DC Green Party were listed in time).<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> It is possible that the DC Green Party's 4 delegates will arrive at the National Convention uncommitted.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="North_Carolina">North Carolina</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_presidential_primaries,_2016&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: North Carolina">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>This state's Green Party held its presidential preference vote on June 25.
</p><p>Jill Stein won this state's presidential preference vote, and will receive all of its delegates.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nebraska_convention">Nebraska convention</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_presidential_primaries,_2016&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Nebraska convention">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Nebraska Green Party held its state convention on June 26 in <a href="/wiki/Lincoln,_Nebraska" title="Lincoln, Nebraska">Lincoln, Nebraska</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Jill Stein won the presidential preference vote at the Nebraska Green Party's state convention. Stein will receive all 4 of Nebraska's delegates.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Iowa_primary">Iowa primary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_presidential_primaries,_2016&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Iowa primary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>All registered Greens were mailed a presidential primary ballot. After all ballots were returned, the ballots were counted publicly at the <a href="/wiki/Iowa_City" class="mw-redirect" title="Iowa City">Iowa City</a> Public Library on July 9.
</p><p>Jill Stein won the Iowa primary, and received 3 out of the 4 available delegates. William Kreml received the other delegate.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="West_Virginia_convention">West Virginia convention</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_presidential_primaries,_2016&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: West Virginia convention">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Mountain Party designated their four delegates at their convention on July 16 in <a href="/wiki/Bridgeport,_West_Virginia" title="Bridgeport, West Virginia">Bridgeport, West Virginia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Jill_Stein" title="Jill Stein">Jill Stein</a> received all four delegates from West Virginia.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Louisiana">Louisiana</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_presidential_primaries,_2016&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Louisiana">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>This state's Green Party held its presidential preference vote on July 30.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Michigan_convention">Michigan convention</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_presidential_primaries,_2016&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Michigan convention">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Michigan Green Party held a state meeting to select delegates to send to the national convention on May 19.  It will hold its state convention to select its presidential preference and other candidates on July 30 and 31 in <a href="/wiki/Lansing,_Michigan" title="Lansing, Michigan">Lansing, Michigan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Florida_primary">Florida primary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_presidential_primaries,_2016&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Florida primary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Green Party of Florida held their primary on July 31, 2016. Early voting began on July 25.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>  On July 31, 2016, the Green Party of Florida announced that Jill Stein had won the Florida primary using <a href="/wiki/Instant-runoff_voting" title="Instant-runoff voting">instant-runoff voting</a>.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arkansas_delegation">Arkansas delegation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_presidential_primaries,_2016&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Arkansas delegation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Arkansas sent delegates to the National Convention without holding a primary, caucus, or convention. Instead, Arkansas's delegates pledged themselves to the presumptive nominee based on the number of delegates each candidate received over the course of the primaries. Jill Stein had the most delegates by a wide margin, therefore Arkansas's delegates voted for her at the convention.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Debates">Debates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Party_presidential_primaries,_2016&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Debates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_presidential_debates_and_forums,_2016" title="Green Party presidential debates and forums, 2016">Green Party presidential debates and forums, 2016</a></div>
<p>The Green Party of New Mexico and <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.abqpeaceandjustice.org/index.php/about/pajola/item/341-students-organizing-action-for-peace-soap">Students Organizing Action for Peace</a> hosted a debate on April 9 at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_New_Mexico" title="University of New Mexico">University of New Mexico</a>'s Student Union Building. The debate was streamed online through Burque Media Productions. All five candidates recognized by the national party were invited.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/RT_America" title="RT America">RT America</a> announced that it would broadcast a Green Party presidential debate on May 9, 2016, featuring Green Party candidates Jill Stein, Kent Mesplay and Sedinam Kinamo Christin Moyowasifza Curry.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>  The debate was moderated by the hosts of the RT America program <i>Watching the Hawks</i>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tyrel_Ventura&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Tyrel Ventura (page does not exist)">Tyrel Ventura</a> and Tabetha Wallace.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> The debate is available on <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a> as <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=tw6LeHRrEvk">RT America’s 2016 Green Party Debate</a>.
</p>
